  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_24ac007e-082d-4f86-97e4-269a4ba0950b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer11709881774390872667">Stark lives in Colour, a neighbourhood whose inhabitants like to be co-ordinated with their surroundings – a neighbourhood where spangly purple trousers are admired by the walls of buildings as you pass them. Close by is Sound, where you mustn’t make any, apart from one designated hour a day when you can scream your lungs raw. Then there’s Red – get off at Fuck Station Zer</span>
  <span id="freeText11709881774390872667" style="display:none">Stark lives in Colour, a neighbourhood whose inhabitants like to be co-ordinated with their surroundings – a neighbourhood where spangly purple trousers are admired by the walls of buildings as you pass them. Close by is Sound, where you mustn’t make any, apart from one designated hour a day when you can scream your lungs raw. Then there’s Red – get off at Fuck Station Zero if you want to see a tactical nuclear battle recreated as a sales demonstration.<br /><br />Stark has friends in Red, which is just as well because Something is about to happen. And when a Something happens it’s no good chanting ‘Duck and cover’ while cowering in a corner, because a Something is always from the past, Stark’s past, and it won’t go away until you face it full on.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The entire book reads like Smith was writing without an outline and just let things happen. As a result the book is full of things that don't make sen<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The entire book reads like Smith was writing without an outline and just let things happen. As a result the book is full of things that don't make sense. This is simply another one. Even Smith couldn't couldn't answer this question because I guarantee you isn't something he gave any thought to. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_458512080" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/458512080" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/458512080?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781931081184" href="/book/show/280803.Only_Forward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=awards">awards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=should-buy">should-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library-kindle">my-library-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=mindbender">mindbender</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458512080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6338822561755860042"><b>"I made a mental note to tell the next Street Engineer I met that they were doing a damn fine job. Sort of an embarrassing thing to think, but I knew it was safe; I always lose my mental notes."<br/></b><br/>Glad I'm not the only one. I had some intelligent things to say about <i>Only Forward,</i> but I can't find my mental sticky notes. I do know that I found the beginning undeniably clever and almost unputdownable. My reading updates show chuckling and snerking through the first hundred pages.<br/><b><br/>"Working out what tha</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6338822561755860042" style="display:none"><b>"I made a mental note to tell the next Street Engineer I met that they were doing a damn fine job. Sort of an embarrassing thing to think, but I knew it was safe; I always lose my mental notes."<br /></b><br />Glad I'm not the only one. I had some intelligent things to say about <i>Only Forward,</i> but I can't find my mental sticky notes. I do know that I found the beginning undeniably clever and almost unputdownable. My reading updates show chuckling and snerking through the first hundred pages.<br /><b><br />"Working out what that might be was going to be important, and I put a memo in my mental file to have a crack at it when I could be bothered. My mental memos are different from my mental notes: I always do something about them eventually, and they're typed so I can read what they say."<br /></b><br />And then suddenly my updates stopped, because, damn, that shit started to get real, going from world-weary, cynical humor to semi-thriller to something deeper and more devastating.<br /><b><br />"I could defend myself, say it isn't easy... but I won't, because that's not the point. The point is too deep, too personal and too small to explain. The point is not for spectators. Nothing that's important, really important, looks impressive, because it only means something to the person that does it. Staying alive, for example, not dying: it looks so easy, but sometimes it's almost too difficult to be borne."<br /></b><br />A really good book that is unlike most things I've read, but perhaps similar in tone and scope to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3007704.The_Gone_Away_World_" title="The Gone-Away World  by Nick Harkaway" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gone-Away World</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6720404.Cursed" title="Cursed by Jeremy C. Shipp" rel="nofollow noopener">Cursed</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3191189.Pandemonium" title="Pandemonium by Daryl Gregory" rel="nofollow noopener">Pandemonium</a>. Probably some people might feel there is a similarity with Vonnegut, but it's been a very long time since I read him, and I found Stark to be far more accessible than any of Vonnegut's characters. All take a skewed view of the world, people sort of making connections and an emotional undercurrent to make something quite interesting. First published in 1994, it feels amazingly current in 2017. Note: also an award winner, with the British Fantasy Award in 1995 and the Philip K. Dick award in 2000.<br /><br />Set in a Britain of the future, it is one we can almost recognize, where cities have become something like gated communities known as Neighborhoods, where people of a kind can band together and really support what they believe in. Some of these cities make perfect sense, such as Idyll, <b>"an old Neighborhood, where people come and go quietly and peacefully. They don't care about anyone else, and they have no argument with anyone. They just want to be left alone to be kind and gentle to each other. I know that sounds kind of weird, but it works for them." </b>Some are just futuristically weird, like Color, where the narrator, Stark lives. Color has color rules, including a strict after-dark black jacket code.<br /><br />Someone who is clearly quite important to Stark, although it isn't exactly clear how or why, asks him for a favor, to find someone who has gone missing from the Type A Neighborhood. It is unprecedented, and while Stark wonders "which kind of job this might be," it seems straightforward so he agrees.<br /><br />Much of the story is like that; Smith tells us what we need to know, but we know Stark is holding things back. And that's fine. He's wit is as dry as pixie dust, but it's as funny as hell. For instance, take his description of trying to answer the phone:<br /><b><br />"It was a long and arduous journey, full of trials, setbacks and heroic derring-do on my part. I was almost there, for example, when I ran out of cigarettes, and had to go back to fetch another packet."<br /></b><br />Then there's catching up with an old friend:<br /><b><br />"We chewed the rag for a while. I recapped the last few months, mentioned a couple of mutual acquaintances I'd run into. Ji told me his land had expanded another half mile to the north, which explained his bars continued existence, recounted a couple of especially horrific successes and used the word "fuck" just over 400 times."<br /></b><br />At his business meeting:<br /><b><br />"'Uh-huh,' I said, reeling under the impact of so much bad film dialogue. "So put a trace on him. "<br /></b><br />The humor eventually fades somewhat, leaving a different, more emotionally sincere tone in its wake. It ended up having more of an emotional impact than I expected, particularly for a book that had me giggling through the beginning.<br /><br />Visiting different Neighborhoods gives Stark a chance to engage in entertaining social commentary. It's soon apparent Mr. A has left his Neighborhood, which means we get to visit some of the other ones nearby. The world-building doesn't make a ton of literal sense; I suppose one could think of it as metaphorical, and indeed it is a commentary on how we choose to live with those like us, but his vision is also extremely interesting.<br /><br />I unquestionably enjoyed it most of the way through, but found the ending... not at all what I expected. It took a turn that didn't entirely work for me and called into question most of the preceding story. That's an unsettling feeling to have in a book, but I think it was unsettling in a good way, raising questions about authorial intent, narrators, etc. Wastrel has a nice analysis of the book. I admit, most of that didn't occur to me when reading, which is, I think, the better kind of revolutionary story. It was only much later after reading that I thought of the Vonnegut comparison, who honestly, was kind of a chore in high school, even when I read him for fun. I actually started re-reading this all over again, enjoying it just as much. One of those book you keep thinking about after finishing. Read at your own risk.<br /><br />Four and a half stars, rounding up, because there aren't many books I remember so well three months after finishing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6338822561755860042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Followed by completely ignoring x, y and z, and throwing in a straightforward explanation of what has actually been going on the whole time.<br/><br/>I really, really liked the explanation, but the book forgot to tell a compelling story un</span>
  <span id="freeText7462446102063473852" style="display:none">Conceptually it's brilliant, but with terrible execution and poor writing.<br /><br />95% of it is "Ohh look at x isn't it WEIRD?! Actually, never mind, how about y, isn't y WEIRD?! Well, if you think y is weird, you're really going to go wild for z! It's the weirdest of them all!" Followed by completely ignoring x, y and z, and throwing in a straightforward explanation of what has actually been going on the whole time.<br /><br />I really, really liked the explanation, but the book forgot to tell a compelling story until the last 20 pages or so. I would LOVE this book if someone took the main premise and rewrote it in a way that was compelling.</span>

<div id="review_63107968" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63107968" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63107968?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=multiple-award-winners">multiple-award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=6-star-books">6-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=love-those-words">love-those-words</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=multiple-award-nominee">multiple-award-nominee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-nominee-philip-k-dick">award-nominee-philip-k-dick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=cyber-punk-prep-and-post">cyber-punk-prep-and-post</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-winner-philip-k-dick">award-winner-philip-k-dick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=1990-1999">1990-1999</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63107968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6722818246096610334">6.0 stars. On my list of "All Time Favorite" novels. I really enjoyed the two other books I have read by Michael Marshall Smith, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21010.Spares' title='Spares by Michael Marshall Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Spares</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/128642.Straw_Men' title='Straw Men by Michael Marshall Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Straw Men</a> and so had fairly high expections going into this book. They were SIGNIFICANTLY exceeded. I loved this book from the opening page to the very last word. <br/><br/>This book is defintely a "mind trip" where reality is not always what you think it is and you are never sure what is going to happen next. However, unlike other books like this, the author does a s</span>
  <span id="freeText6722818246096610334" style="display:none">6.0 stars. On my list of "All Time Favorite" novels. I really enjoyed the two other books I have read by Michael Marshall Smith, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21010.Spares" title="Spares by Michael Marshall Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">Spares</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/128642.Straw_Men" title="Straw Men by Michael Marshall Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">Straw Men</a> and so had fairly high expections going into this book. They were SIGNIFICANTLY exceeded. I loved this book from the opening page to the very last word. <br /><br />This book is defintely a "mind trip" where reality is not always what you think it is and you are never sure what is going to happen next. However, unlike other books like this, the author does a superb job of never losing his audience. You always have enough of an understanding to follow the story and, most importantly, you know that the explanations are coming. That is always a big issue for me when I am reading a story like this. If everything is not clear enough to follow the story line, I get distracted by finding myself asking, "Did I miss something" and wondering if I need to go back a reread the what I have already read. That usually leads to frustration and lack of "immersion" in the story if it goes on for too long. That does not happen here where the author does a great job of having his main character, Stark, basically tell you "look you are not going to understand this now, but I will explain it to you later if its necessary so sit back and just trust me for the moment...." By doing this he let's you know to enjoy the ride and everything will be made clear at the appropriate time, which it eventually is. I thought this was brilliant.<br /><br />In addition to having an incredibly original, mind-blowing plot, this book has some absolutely amazing characters starting with the protaganist, Stark, who is a private investigator handling very "unique" matters. Add to that a couple of psychotic, but well mannered brothers, Ji and Sneed, a couple of sarcatic "home applicances" and cat that gives any dog a run for its money as "man's best friend" and you have the makings for a dark, funny and, in the end, very poignant story. Stark's narration throughout is brilliant. He is both very funny (I laughed out loud more than once) and yet is able to grab you when the emotional aspects of the story become more serious. His tone was just perfect. <br /><br />Anyway, as you can tell from my comments above, I LOVED THIS BOOK. It receives my HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!!!<br /><br />Winner: British Fantasy Award<br />Winner: Philip K. Dick Award </span>
  <a data-text-id="6722818246096610334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2319368278" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319368278" />
    <a title="Jack Tripper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35473855-jack-tripper"><img alt="Jack Tripper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484547420p2/35473855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319368278?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Tripper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Tripper" href="/user/show/35473855-jack-tripper">Jack Tripper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553579703" href="/book/show/128645.Only_Forward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=weird">weird</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=cyberpunk">cyberpunk</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319368278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9754135046814898277">(Full review 3/25/18)<br/><br/>What starts out as a hilarious send-up of cyberpunk and hardboiled/noir eventually turns into a hallucinatory nightmare, making it almost two novels in one. If Neal Stephenson's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/603262.Snow_Crash' title='Snow Crash by Neal Stephenson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Snow Crash</a> was cyberpunk-cubed, with loads more action and craziness than your typical Gibson-esque fare, then this is <i>Snow Crash</i>-cubed, at least in the earlier sections. It would have been fine had it kept its initial tone throughout, but the second half takes everything to another level.<br/><br/>It takes pl</span>
  <span id="freeText9754135046814898277" style="display:none">(Full review 3/25/18)<br /><br />What starts out as a hilarious send-up of cyberpunk and hardboiled/noir eventually turns into a hallucinatory nightmare, making it almost two novels in one. If Neal Stephenson's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/603262.Snow_Crash" title="Snow Crash by Neal Stephenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Snow Crash</a> was cyberpunk-cubed, with loads more action and craziness than your typical Gibson-esque fare, then this is <i>Snow Crash</i>-cubed, at least in the earlier sections. It would have been fine had it kept its initial tone throughout, but the second half takes everything to another level.<br /><br />It takes place in the far future, in a giant city that's as big as a country basically, but it's divided up into various neighborhoods that are entirely different from one other, even blocked off from each other sometimes. One neighborhood is for busybody workoholics, who do nothing but run around their offices 20 hours or so a day. Another is for people really into color, and the buildings color coordinate themselves on the fly to whatever the people on the street are wearing. One particular neighborhood has no idea other neighborhoods exist, as the walls surrounding it are covered in projection screens showing an apocalyptic wasteland outside. Another is nothing but gang warfare at all times. Et cetera.<br /><br />The story's told in first-person by Stark, who's from Color neighborhood, and his job is finding things. That's it. And he's really good at it. The higher-ups in the Type-A personality/workoholic community have tasked Stark with finding one of their own who's gone missing in a suspected kidnapping, and what seems like a simple enough job somehow becomes a twisted mindbender of a journey in a surrealistic dream-like world where absolutely anything can happen and your worst fears may be realized, in horrifyingly nightmarish form. And that's all I'll say about that. Best for the reader to discover it themselves.<br /><br />The problem is that I had NO idea this was the case, and when I first tried reading this several years ago, I set it down a couple chapters in, as I wasn't really in the mood for a comedic post-cyberpunk adventure at the time. If only I'd known. Comedy, sf, horror, fantasy, noir -- this book has it all, and it's pulled off to near-perfection. It's just plain fun to read, and Stark makes for an engaging, hilarious narrator. Until now I'd stuck with Michael Marshall Smith's excellent short horror fiction, but that will certainly change. Brilliant.<br /><br />4.5 Stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9754135046814898277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_581253420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581253420" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/581253420?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=cyberpunk">cyberpunk</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer581253420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1695592316212568640">Oh -- my -- god. When I started reading this book I expected it to keep up the fairly light tone of the early chapters. Then it fucked with my heart bad. Don't believe reviews saying it makes no sense: it makes perfect sense, in the end, as long as you stop holding onto normal logic and start applying some dream logic. The narrator is unreliable, yeah, and he has attitude, and he knows he's telling a story, so there are bits that some people find irritating, like the way he keeps saying he'll te</span>
  <span id="freeText1695592316212568640" style="display:none">Oh -- my -- god. When I started reading this book I expected it to keep up the fairly light tone of the early chapters. Then it fucked with my heart bad. Don't believe reviews saying it makes no sense: it makes perfect sense, in the end, as long as you stop holding onto normal logic and start applying some dream logic. The narrator is unreliable, yeah, and he has attitude, and he knows he's telling a story, so there are bits that some people find irritating, like the way he keeps saying he'll tell us more about [whatever] later, if it's relevant. And I can understand that, but for me it's all part of who the narrator is.<br /><br />I love the world built up here. The different neighbourhoods, the cats, the whys and wherefores of The City. I love the writing, because so much of it is painfully on the nose about trauma, about the demons we're capable of dreaming up. I love all of this more than I love the characters, really: I love it for what it has to say about trauma, about the way we think.<br /><br />It's hard to talk about it without any spoilers, really. All I can say is that it comes together in the end, and you understand things in a heartbreaking rush, and it really is good. Weird, yes. But very good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1695592316212568640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vit Babenco" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vit Babenco" href="/user/show/19283284-vit-babenco">Vit Babenco</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553579703" href="/book/show/128645.Only_Forward">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1878786048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15782662816715839748"><b>Michael Marshall Smith</b> combines dystopia, hardboiled mystery and magic realism but he is always staying on the mocking side of things so the black humour fountains up.<br/>The dystopian world is sinister and kitschy:<br/>“There's no good or bad time to get on a Red mono. They don't have hours where you do certain things, or days even. You just pay your money and take your chances. Actually, by Red standards the carriage I boarded was fairly civilised. True, there was both vomit and a human turd on the sea</span>
  <span id="freeText15782662816715839748" style="display:none"><b>Michael Marshall Smith</b> combines dystopia, hardboiled mystery and magic realism but he is always staying on the mocking side of things so the black humour fountains up.<br />The dystopian world is sinister and kitschy:<br />“There's no good or bad time to get on a Red mono. They don't have hours where you do certain things, or days even. You just pay your money and take your chances. Actually, by Red standards the carriage I boarded was fairly civilised. True, there was both vomit and a human turd on the seat next to mine, but I've seen worse. The prostitutes were mainly too stoned to be doing serious business, the fight down the end was over very quickly, and there were never more than two dead bodies in the carriage at any one time.”<br />The private eye is tougher than a crowd of cartoon superheroes:<br />“Every face says something: the deal with mine is that though you might not like what it's saying you have to admire the strength of its convictions.”<br />And his dreams come true:<br />“I'm where I am now because when I was young I wanted more. I wanted to live in a film. I looked, and I found. Now I live in that film, and here the bad guys are everyone who isn't you and if they die you don't have to give a damn.”<br />And magic realism turns into a bad psychedelic trip:<br />“When I turned they all stepped out and doubled up with laughter, pointing at me. Dismayed, I turned back to the King, but he was laughing too. I whirled back to face the crowd again and they were still pointing and laughing, and then suddenly they were all chanting ‘We can see your bottom, we can see your bottom,’ and I looked down to see I was naked. I put my hands in front of me and turned once more to the King. He was still laughing, laughing harder and harder, his upper body whipping up and down so fast his head was a blur.”<br />It grotesquely resembles <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland__Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___1_" title="Alice in Wonderland (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, #1) by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Wonderland</a>, which finally transforms into Horrorland and then everything turns very serious… <br />There is no end of imaginary worlds but there is the only one real world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15782662816715839748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3153431731" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3153431731" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3153431731?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/53587416-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3153431731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3008318316805136315">What a wonderfully weird, touching and inspired story. The first half was rough - a noir style detective story with writing I found flat and wholly unsubtle, and humor that mostly missed the mark. It was almost a DNF.<br/><br/>Yet, the second half takes on whole new dimensions, not even hinted at earlier. The story weaves together elements of magical realism and alternate realities that mix and blend in bizarre, dreamlike ways that feel bewildering but also strangely compelling. Think what the film Incept</span>
  <span id="freeText3008318316805136315" style="display:none">What a wonderfully weird, touching and inspired story. The first half was rough - a noir style detective story with writing I found flat and wholly unsubtle, and humor that mostly missed the mark. It was almost a DNF.<br /><br />Yet, the second half takes on whole new dimensions, not even hinted at earlier. The story weaves together elements of magical realism and alternate realities that mix and blend in bizarre, dreamlike ways that feel bewildering but also strangely compelling. Think what the film Inception might be like if it was written by China Mieville or Lavie Tidhar. The writing also gets remarkably better, and darker, as the story progresses. More profound, evocative and marked with real emotional depth.<br /><br />At the beginning you think this is a kind of noir style detective story in a strange, yet comprehensible version of the future. Yet it becomes so much more. A journey of personal growth, with depth and soul, in a world that's bizarre and dark, filled equally with horror and wonder. Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3008318316805136315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_340431772" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/340431772" />
    <a title="Ryandake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4057623-ryandake"><img alt="Ryandake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280111549p2/4057623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/340431772?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryandake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryandake" href="/user/show/4057623-ryandake">Ryandake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer340431772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1599411374758467826">i want to take a pair of scissors to this book.<br/><br/>not to make confetti, or compost, of it, but to rearrange it.<br/><br/>the author is introducing <i>quite central</i> new characters on page 320, fer chrissakes! the last 15 or so pages of the book are a firehose of infodump (well-written infodump, but still), the streams of which tie the book together.<br/><br/>but how much better it could have been if those streams were introduced earlier as rills... it would have ameliorated the worst problems of the beginning, and made th</span>
  <span id="freeText1599411374758467826" style="display:none">i want to take a pair of scissors to this book.<br /><br />not to make confetti, or compost, of it, but to rearrange it.<br /><br />the author is introducing <i>quite central</i> new characters on page 320, fer chrissakes! the last 15 or so pages of the book are a firehose of infodump (well-written infodump, but still), the streams of which tie the book together.<br /><br />but how much better it could have been if those streams were introduced earlier as rills... it would have ameliorated the worst problems of the beginning, and made the end vastly more emotionally intense.<br /><br />ok wait. begin at the beginning.<br /><br />our protag, Stark, is a rather noir-ish, trash-talking, gun-waving tracker of lost people and other things. he gets a call from Zenda, a woman with whom he's had some past, and she propels him on the assignment that is the central plot of this novel. mostly. sort of.<br /><br />Stark's world is not our world--it's a sort of reified version of contemporary digital villages. people cluster together by affinities, allowing cross-pollination to varying degrees. this does give the book some gleeful energy, but ultimately does not seem meaningful to the central dilemmas of the characters. it's window-dressing; really good window-dressing sometimes, but not an integral part of the writing.<br /><br />anyway. it's a mystery, for a while; a thriller, for a while; a metaphysical/psychological puzzle, for a while; and for 15 or so pages at the end, an attempt at being a tear-jerker. a kind of frankenstein of a book, in a way--the parts don't always seem to fit.<br /><br />but i still want to rearrange it into cohesion.<br /><br />it's not a bad read, but it can be a frustration to read a decently-written book and know that it could have been vastly better with some editorial attention. Smith needed a Gordon Lish, at least as an advisor. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1599411374758467826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3730519627014501184">Weird. Really. Hard to classify too. The first half of the book follows Stark, who is hired to find an important person, who is believed to have been kidnapped. He lives in an interesting alternative world, with many oddball friends and neighborhoods, my favorite of which is the Cat Neighborhood. About halfway through, everything changes as we are abruptly transitioned into a dreamworld, with little upfront explanation. As the explanation unfolds bit by bit, we long for a cohesive end. There is </span>
  <span id="freeText3730519627014501184" style="display:none">Weird. Really. Hard to classify too. The first half of the book follows Stark, who is hired to find an important person, who is believed to have been kidnapped. He lives in an interesting alternative world, with many oddball friends and neighborhoods, my favorite of which is the Cat Neighborhood. About halfway through, everything changes as we are abruptly transitioned into a dreamworld, with little upfront explanation. As the explanation unfolds bit by bit, we long for a cohesive end. There is an ending, but it was unsatisfying as we learned how Stark became who he is. Perhaps most frustrating, at least to me, was the introduction of central and pivotal characters in the last 20-25 pages.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2020">2020</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3196759096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6615530155725638449">What an odd gem this book is. It starts out as an entertaining thriller set in a unique near-future world. I was digging it immensely, especially because the main protagonist, Stark, is extremely engaging. He was a perfect mix of humor and can-do that makes for some great lines.<br/><br/>For instance:<br/><br/>"[T]he stations zipped by soundlessly, and I geared myself up for whatever it was I had to gear myself up for. I didn’t have much to go on, so I just geared up generally."<br/><br/>Talking about not wanting to remember</span>
  <span id="freeText6615530155725638449" style="display:none">What an odd gem this book is. It starts out as an entertaining thriller set in a unique near-future world. I was digging it immensely, especially because the main protagonist, Stark, is extremely engaging. He was a perfect mix of humor and can-do that makes for some great lines.<br /><br />For instance:<br /><br />"[T]he stations zipped by soundlessly, and I geared myself up for whatever it was I had to gear myself up for. I didn’t have much to go on, so I just geared up generally."<br /><br />Talking about not wanting to remember a thing: "but I knew I was safe: I always lose my mental notes."<br /><br />On the topic of a long wait at a restaurant: "Then finally, like some optical illusion, the art student reappeared. I found myself frankly incredulous that she didn’t now have grey hair and walk with a stoop, and decided it must be her great-granddaughter bringing my order, concluding an ancient and mystic hereditary task passed down the family line."<br /><br />Finally:<br /><br />"Life is like a video game: when you get to a new screen, the thing to do is move as quickly as possible, before the situation gets any worse."<br /><br />Then, about 50% of the way through (exactly 50% on my Kindle actually), this book gets weird. Your thriller is turned on its head and we go to dreamland...erm...Jeamland. <br /><br />It almost lost me at that point if I'm being honest. <br /><br />Luckily, I stuck with it, probably mostly because of the protagonist, because the weird doesn't let up, but the dreamland is really kind of a cool idea. I can see not everyone jiving with the ideas presented, but I finally grew to really like it.<br /><br />Then, there are some well-done last-minute twists that sealed the deal on top of everything.<br /><br />I don't want to give away too much. My recommendation, give it a go and push through the weird bit. It does put the whole story on its head, but I thought it worked.<br /><br />4 out of 5 Stars (highly recommended)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6615530155725638449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12442064660825026653">Brought to your courtesy of Reading Project 2015.<br/><br/>I love this, I deeply love it, largely because of a single quote which I shall now transcribe:<br/><br/><blockquote>How many times have you tried to talk to someone about something that matters to you, tried to get them to see it the way you do? And how many of those times have ended with you feeling bitter, resenting them for making you feel like your pain doesn't have any substance after all?<br/><br/>Like when you've split up with someone, and you try to communicate the way y</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12442064660825026653" style="display:none">Brought to your courtesy of Reading Project 2015.<br /><br />I love this, I deeply love it, largely because of a single quote which I shall now transcribe:<br /><br /><blockquote>How many times have you tried to talk to someone about something that matters to you, tried to get them to see it the way you do? And how many of those times have ended with you feeling bitter, resenting them for making you feel like your pain doesn't have any substance after all?<br /><br />Like when you've split up with someone, and you try to communicate the way you feel, because you need to say the words, need to feel that somebody understands just how pissed off and frightened you feel. The problem is, they never do. "Plenty more fish in the sea," they'll say, or "You're better off without them," or "Do you want some of these potato chips?" They never really understand, because they haven't been there, every day, every hour. They don't know the way things have been, the way that it's made you, the way it has structured your world. They'll never realise that someone who makes you feel bad may be the person you need most in the world. They don't understand the history, the background, don't know the pillars of memory that hold you up. Ultimately, they don't know you well enough, and they never can. Everyone's alone in their world, because everybody's life is different. You can send people letters, and show them photos, but they can never come to visit where you live.<br /><br />Unless you love them. And then they can burn it down.</blockquote><br /><br />So, yes, deeply love but not much actual memory of ... y'know ... what the book is about or what happens in it.<br /><br />I seem to remember the narrator actively lies which is a new level of unreliability.<br /><br />Mind-twisty and intriguing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12442064660825026653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1147756299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1147756299" />
    <a title="Adam Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7004622-adam-light"><img alt="Adam Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481355960p2/7004622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1147756299?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Light" href="/user/show/7004622-adam-light">Adam Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=2015-january">2015-january</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=my-personal-favorites">my-personal-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=bizarre">bizarre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=best-reads-of-2014">best-reads-of-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=michael-marshall-smith">michael-marshall-smith</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1147756299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15206693007236292336">ONLY FORWARD is one of the most original, mind-bending novels I have had the pleasure to read in as long as I can remember.<br/><br/>I planned to read it sometime this year, but when I put it on my to-read list, my friend Gregor promptly advised me that this deserved my immediate attention.<br/><br/>To begin with, I read the Straw Men trilogy by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2954265.Michael_Marshall' title='Michael Marshall' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michael Marshall</a>many years ago, and had no idea that the masterful author of those books also wrote under the name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12339.Michael_Marshall_Smith' title='Michael Marshall Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michael Marshall Smith</a>. When I learned this, I sought out</span>
  <span id="freeText15206693007236292336" style="display:none">ONLY FORWARD is one of the most original, mind-bending novels I have had the pleasure to read in as long as I can remember.<br /><br />I planned to read it sometime this year, but when I put it on my to-read list, my friend Gregor promptly advised me that this deserved my immediate attention.<br /><br />To begin with, I read the Straw Men trilogy by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2954265.Michael_Marshall" title="Michael Marshall" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Marshall</a>many years ago, and had no idea that the masterful author of those books also wrote under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12339.Michael_Marshall_Smith" title="Michael Marshall Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Marshall Smith</a>. When I learned this, I sought out books he had written under this name.<br /><br />According to the author, ONLY FORWARD was his first book, and he set no limits, and he personally warned me to set aside expectations. I did so, gladly.<br /><br />This book blew away everything I've read in a long time. It was so surreal, but the amazing part was that no matter how strange and hallucinatory it became, it never bogged down, got confusing or lost my interest. It never felt forced. It flowed with the consistency of a dream. I was so intrigued, I read it in two days. Couldn't put it down for anything.<br /><br />Only Forward is narrated by Stark, a guy who takes care of things that need taken care of. He is a very likeable, yet unreliable character; he seems to have a lot of secrets. He often states that there might be something we might need to know, but he isn't going to waste our time talking about it unless it becomes relevant.<br /><br />Stark takes on a job that involved finding a very important man who has apparently been kidnapped.<br /><br />There is the smell of conspiracy right away.<br /><br />I'm not going to say anything else. This just needs to be read.<br /><br /><br />What really got me was when part two began. It was about halfway through the book. I was so impressed with how Smith pulled this off, I could not stop reading it. Very cool.<br /><br />I have this one on the must read again list. It was that good.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15206693007236292336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_77341185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/810550-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810550-bill?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77341185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3123604181258048775">This is probably going to be the worst review I've written.<br/>There is so much to say about this novel, but I can't really tell you anything without spoiling it. <br/>So, where to start?<br/>How about the story? Well, the less you know, the better. Suffice it to say, our hero's travels take on some strange turns.<br/><br/>This is the second book I've read by Smith. His thriller Straw Men, under the name Michael Smith, was quite good, but the story wasn't one I wanted to keep following for two more novels. <br/><br/>Only Forward</span>
  <span id="freeText3123604181258048775" style="display:none">This is probably going to be the worst review I've written.<br />There is so much to say about this novel, but I can't really tell you anything without spoiling it. <br />So, where to start?<br />How about the story? Well, the less you know, the better. Suffice it to say, our hero's travels take on some strange turns.<br /><br />This is the second book I've read by Smith. His thriller Straw Men, under the name Michael Smith, was quite good, but the story wasn't one I wanted to keep following for two more novels. <br /><br />Only Forward was enough to convince me that I have to read everything else by this guy.<br />Not only was the story outstanding, but this is some of the finest writing you will come across. There were a couple of times he made me laugh out loud, but many more times when he made me marvel at his poignant observances on the human condition.<br />The only thing that irked me was that there were a couple of things that I would have liked explained further, like Cat Neighbourhood, for instance. But maybe he meant to leave that to the imagination.<br /><br />I need to make this a short review, otherwise I'll start ranting and raving and giving too much away.<br /><br />Read Only Forward. It's only 300+ pages, an easy read, and it will take you on a mind trip.<br /><br />Enjoy the ride.<br /></span>

<div id="review_579401506" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579401506" />
    <a title="Daniel Roy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5368477-daniel-roy"><img alt="Daniel Roy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513163643p2/5368477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579401506?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Roy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Roy" href="/user/show/5368477-daniel-roy">Daniel Roy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11277567-only-forward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5368477-daniel-roy?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5368477-daniel-roy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5368477-daniel-roy?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5368477-daniel-roy?shelf=taw-bookclub">taw-bookclub</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579401506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14266897854511465960">What a perplexing book. On the one hand, I certainly have never read anything quite like it; but then there are tons of aspects of the book that are irritating and unsatisfying, making the novel fall well short of brilliance.<br/><br/>The novel starts as an <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams' title='Douglas Adams' rel='nofollow noopener'>Adams</a>-esque science fictional satire, complete with home appliances with snappy personalities. My suspension of disbelief wrestled with the setting for a while, until I accepted that it was satirical and surreal, and thus should not be expected to make</span>
  <span id="freeText14266897854511465960" style="display:none">What a perplexing book. On the one hand, I certainly have never read anything quite like it; but then there are tons of aspects of the book that are irritating and unsatisfying, making the novel fall well short of brilliance.<br /><br />The novel starts as an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams" title="Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">Adams</a>-esque science fictional satire, complete with home appliances with snappy personalities. My suspension of disbelief wrestled with the setting for a while, until I accepted that it was satirical and surreal, and thus should not be expected to make much sense. I wouldn't have thought much of this book if that was all there was to it; but I stuck with it because some reviews mentioned that the story went somewhere unexpected. And boy, did it ever.<br /><br />The second part of the novel starts to build a much-needed sense of gravitas, and takes a turn for the psychological. There are parts of it that qualify as horror, inasmuch as there is plenty of graphical descriptions of bodily fluids; but besides a frightening nightmare chase, not much of the horror elements resonated much with me.<br /><br />The setting, though, became compelling and exciting. Smith captures the disjointed emotional landscape of dreams with brio. I tend to read in bed, and there were many moments where I had to perform a <a href="http://lucid.wikia.com/wiki/Reality_check" rel="nofollow noopener">reality check</a> to make sure the surreal, liquid prose wasn't the result of having fallen asleep and dreaming that I'm reading a book.<br /><br />Ultimately, though, even the brilliance of this sequence isn't enough to rescue a scattered plot. The prose is sometimes flat, sometimes brilliant, but none of the characters really transcend hard-boiled stock. The novel feels as if Mr. Smith was carrying three book outlines down the stairs, tripped, and picked up the pages again. The story builds to an emotional catharsis near the end, but it does so by dumping background information on the reader in the last twenty-five pages of the novel.<br /><br />All in all, a perplexing book. Quite unique, but not all for the right reasons.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14266897854511465960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103145503" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3656911-sammie?shelf=age-over-10">age-over-10</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103145503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4875870525047939173">This book is exactly what science-fiction should be!<br/><br/>There are two very distinct parts to it. I found the first part (the Neighborhoods) so absorbing, interesting and real that it didn't feel like reading fiction at all. As clichéd as it might sound, I felt like I was really <i>there</i>. The second part of the book (Jeamland) was equally as interesting, thought-provoking and easy to read, but it did not have the same intense feel to it. Plot-wise, Jeamland is a bit of a leap and expects the reader to w</span>
  <span id="freeText4875870525047939173" style="display:none">This book is exactly what science-fiction should be!<br /><br />There are two very distinct parts to it. I found the first part (the Neighborhoods) so absorbing, interesting and real that it didn't feel like reading fiction at all. As clichéd as it might sound, I felt like I was really <i>there</i>. The second part of the book (Jeamland) was equally as interesting, thought-provoking and easy to read, but it did not have the same intense feel to it. Plot-wise, Jeamland is a bit of a leap and expects the reader to willingly abandon a lot of their previous knowledge of sleeping and dreaming.<br /><br />The idea of the different Neighborhoods was brilliantly executed and very intriguing. I would love to read another book set in this future world, as there is only so much detail that can fit into the one book (leaving room for characters and plot, of course!)<br /><br />If you are the kind of reader who does not like to have a complete change of style and scenery half way though a book, then this would not be for you. If you dislike science-fiction as a genre, this book would also probably not be right for you. Otherwise, I see no reason how anyone could read this and not fall in love with it like I did.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4875870525047939173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naomi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naomi" href="/user/show/2282835-naomi">Naomi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177784287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3106178723769592268">Hmmm... this was 4.5 stars...rounding was a challenge. Could have gone up to 5 or down to 3.5. <br/><br/>As I've said, I had a hard time rating this one. I had to consider how much I enjoyed it, plus how good I think it was, plus whether I'd recommend it. <br/><br/>So, 5 stars it is, then. I immensely enjoyed the first third and I'd read the whole thing again. I don't regret it at all and I'd recommend it to anyone as long as they don't have a problem with mentions of corpses and canniablism, dead babies in particu</span>
  <span id="freeText3106178723769592268" style="display:none">Hmmm... this was 4.5 stars...rounding was a challenge. Could have gone up to 5 or down to 3.5. <br /><br />As I've said, I had a hard time rating this one. I had to consider how much I enjoyed it, plus how good I think it was, plus whether I'd recommend it. <br /><br />So, 5 stars it is, then. I immensely enjoyed the first third and I'd read the whole thing again. I don't regret it at all and I'd recommend it to anyone as long as they don't have a problem with mentions of corpses and canniablism, dead babies in particular. <br /><br />I might have given it 4 stars, but I thought The End* was perfect.<br />*The End was the chapter title of the epilogue. <br /><br />So! This book was filled with feels. And humor. And technology I wish I had. And gruesome terribleness. Honestly, some people...<br /><br />If you hate cats, you probably shouldn't read this. Then again, if you hate cats, you're probably a terrible person. Unfriend me. If you are just afraid of them, I won't hold that against you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3106178723769592268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2701740400" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2701740400" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29777818-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523931823p2/29777818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2701740400?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/29777818-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30689386-only-forward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=dreams">dreams</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2701740400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14522141854397155526">Like 1.5 stars maybe? <br/><br/>I did not enjoy this book. It was near DNF almost the whole way. There are some really funny lines now and then, but that's not enough to carry a novel. I had just enough curiosity to keep me going to somewhere between 50 - 60%, then I pretty much skimmed from there to 90%, and finally I just couldn't be bothered to even skim anymore.<br/><br/>Bad stuff:<br/>- Action Centre<br/>- Jeamland (dreamland)<br/>- mild meta / surrealist aspects<br/>- cats<br/>- giggling<br/><br/>Good stuff:<br/>- humor<br/>- MC is tolerably likable<br/><br/>The </span>
  <span id="freeText14522141854397155526" style="display:none">Like 1.5 stars maybe? <br /><br />I did not enjoy this book. It was near DNF almost the whole way. There are some really funny lines now and then, but that's not enough to carry a novel. I had just enough curiosity to keep me going to somewhere between 50 - 60%, then I pretty much skimmed from there to 90%, and finally I just couldn't be bothered to even skim anymore.<br /><br />Bad stuff:<br />- Action Centre<br />- Jeamland (dreamland)<br />- mild meta / surrealist aspects<br />- cats<br />- giggling<br /><br />Good stuff:<br />- humor<br />- MC is tolerably likable<br /><br />The writing seemed good on the one hand, though aspects of the structure and storytelling techniques felt vaguely paint-by-number, something the residents of Colour might appreciate. But this book's main failing was that it really never gave me anything to care about.<br /><br />As I mentioned, there are a lot of good lines throughout the book and I liked the humor, but with a huge caveat. The author builds a world here that seems designed more as a mechanism for social commentary than entertainment, and the section he seems most interested in commenting on for a large chunk of the book, is Action Centre, a stand-in for Type-A Western Capitalist Corporatism. In that aspect perhaps this book would work better for a younger person, someone who still has the energy to spend their free time raging about that stuff. I've worked most of my adult life in Corporate America, and I absolutely loathe it, and I am 100% <i>not interested</i> in some dude's satire of it getting all up in my free time. <i>Even if I agree with his criticism and he makes it funny.</i> Just, no. Get the hell out of my personal space. <br /><br />The author doles out info slowly though, and as I said I was just curious enough to keep going past the point I should have stopped, though I took several side trips to other books as diversions.<br /><br />I can see how some people like this, but it's very much not my thing. Rating rounded down for making me waste way more of my life than I should have on this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14522141854397155526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_269993499" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269993499" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/638550-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399866937p2/638550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269993499?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/638550-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553579703" href="/book/show/128645.Only_Forward">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/638550-daniel?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269993499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7016070476349718356">Early in to this book I flashed back on the books of Ron Goulart that I read back in the 70's and 80's. There was a very similar sense of humor. And as I got a little further in to the book, I began to sense a bit of Phil Dick. When I told this to my friend, he said that the writing style reminded him of Roger Zelazny. I can see that, too.<br/><br/>There was something incredibly unique here. I never got a sense that I was reading something that had been done to death in different ways.<br/><br/>In <em>Only Forward</em>, Smi</span>
  <span id="freeText7016070476349718356" style="display:none">Early in to this book I flashed back on the books of Ron Goulart that I read back in the 70's and 80's. There was a very similar sense of humor. And as I got a little further in to the book, I began to sense a bit of Phil Dick. When I told this to my friend, he said that the writing style reminded him of Roger Zelazny. I can see that, too.<br /><br />There was something incredibly unique here. I never got a sense that I was reading something that had been done to death in different ways.<br /><br />In <em>Only Forward</em>, Smith creates 'Neighborhoods' -- small communities that are named for their own unique, peculiar fetish, and which are difficult to enter and depart from if you are a visitor. One man navigates the Neighborhoods to track down a missing person.<br /><br />The book was fun and intriguing and I was often wondering what was around the next corner.<br /><br />But...only four of five stars because I did feel it was a tad too ambitious. At some point, maybe two-thirds of the way through, I just wanted to get on with the story and have it resolved. It had gone one step too far in uniqueness and I was just a little bored. And then it stepped one more step, which piqued my interest again, and then it resolved. <br /><br />One more stroke of the editor's pen might have made this 5 stars for me, but even so, four stars is a great read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7016070476349718356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Marc Nash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136053-marc-nash"><img alt="Marc Nash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442559977p2/5136053.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
