<div id="review_380104067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380104067" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10765483-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380104067?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/10765483-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10765483-richard?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer380104067&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380104067" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer244028236379719315">I have the distinct feeling that I was either going to adore this book or just not get it at all.<br/><br/>The first half is a science fiction detective novel set in a futuristic city where the majority of the earth's surface is covered in walled "Neighbourhoods". These neighbourhoods have themes and rules that they follow that make them quirky. There's Sound, where no sound is allowed except for one hour a day where people can go into isolation and scream their heads off. Colour, where a curfew for colou</span>
  <span id="freeText244028236379719315" style="display:none">I have the distinct feeling that I was either going to adore this book or just not get it at all.<br /><br />The first half is a science fiction detective novel set in a futuristic city where the majority of the earth's surface is covered in walled "Neighbourhoods". These neighbourhoods have themes and rules that they follow that make them quirky. There's Sound, where no sound is allowed except for one hour a day where people can go into isolation and scream their heads off. Colour, where a curfew for colours is in effect since the, seemingly sentient and reasonable, computer wants to stop changing the scenery to give resident's colour appreciation skills a rest for a while. Others include neighbourhoods almost completely bereft of humans and smaller neighbourhoods where gangs rule and for some reason this utopia won't let people wishing to escape join other neighbourhoods.<br />I'll let this go though since at the time the world existed to me and I was able to believe it.<br /><br />The first quarter or so felt like the author was desperately trying to cram in a joke per line. Thanks to the private detective angle it felt very much like Adams.<br />After the action starts the languages calms down a bit and had me looking forward to an interesting book about conspiracy. Urban fantasy is a thing, there isn't enough light hearted Urban futurism. There are explosions, promising gizmos and you're not really sure who the bad guy is.<br /><br />Unfortunately as soon as they go on the run some foreshadowing about his new companion's nightmares gets brought up and they suddenly decide to go explore the land of dreams to cure them.<br /><br />Yeah.<br /><br />Some interesting things about how dream mechanics work, but then this is all a dream and so nothing really works properly.<br />I followed most of what went on but it seemed to be surreal for the point of being surreal and the trip to the dream world was completely pointless.<br /><br />In the real world they instantly become pursued again and gather their forces to go confront the big bad. Which starts several chapters of info dump, filling in things the main character had left out, lied about or just not bothered to mention before. <br /><br />Having got all this out in the open the bad guy is accepted as a memory or something by the main character and everything fades back to normal. Except his friend, another fairly major character, died really quickly despite being a veteran of the dream world. The monsters that this bad guy left are still floating around dream world messing it up. The client turned out to be ok all along and the attempt to chase and kill them was entirely a misunderstanding. The thing they spend half the novel trying to fix happens anyway. So actually the final confrontation served nothing but closure for the main character to no longer give a crap. <br />Which funnily enough is about what I feel now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="244028236379719315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008117443" href="/book/show/25457124-only-forward">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2084515871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5104858150009177618">Another book club read, and another one where I feel like I'm getting a reputation as the grumpy one. This time, you get my review straight away as I'll be missing the meeting.<br/><br/>So, what to make of it? It's quite entertaining and Stark has a brilliant gift for understatement. I liked some of the areas of The City (ok, mostly just Cat Neighbourhood). The plot is pretty good and the emotional punch of the ending, oh my.<br/><br/>What didn't I like? Well... I get that the different neighbourhoods are meant to </span>
  <span id="freeText5104858150009177618" style="display:none">Another book club read, and another one where I feel like I'm getting a reputation as the grumpy one. This time, you get my review straight away as I'll be missing the meeting.<br /><br />So, what to make of it? It's quite entertaining and Stark has a brilliant gift for understatement. I liked some of the areas of The City (ok, mostly just Cat Neighbourhood). The plot is pretty good and the emotional punch of the ending, oh my.<br /><br />What didn't I like? Well... I get that the different neighbourhoods are meant to be tropey and familiar, but I'm not completely sold on it. In particular, I find myself wondering how the whole neighbourhood system would actually work in practice. Where does the food come from? Who manufactures the ridiculously powerful weapons? How is the place not buried under all the filth you're telling me it leaves in the streets? Especially when whole areas are roofed in from the sky? Probably I should stop overthinking it.<br /><br />The other thing I'm not too keen on is the sexual violence against women. Again, I get that it's kind of part and parcel of the tropes Red is riffing off, but I'm not really wild about how sex slaves are unremarkable wallpaper there. The other chief example would be how the horrific incident (undescribed but implicitly violent sexual assault) that happens to Alkland's sister is only there to give him Man Pain that can be used by others. It's not the need for his guilt that I question, but the method chosen for him to get it.<br /><br />So, overall a mixed bag. I would be leery of recommending it to anyone because of the violence, the gore, the normalised horribleness. But it does have some good points too! I guess I'm wondering why someone would suggest it for a bookclub read though. One of the members seems pretty young...</span>
  <a data-text-id="5104858150009177618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_494034265" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/494034265?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/3081414-laura">Laura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer494034265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15094401607470987024">I hardly know what to think about this book. It started out quite promisingly - an interesting alternative world, solid protagonist and a plot which seemed to be moving at about the right pace. However, around half way through everything changes. This isn't be so bad in and of itself, at least if the rest of the book eventually linked everything together. The problem is that it doesn't. About 20 pages from the end I became extremely suspect when none of the loose ends had been tied up. At this s</span>
  <span id="freeText15094401607470987024" style="display:none">I hardly know what to think about this book. It started out quite promisingly - an interesting alternative world, solid protagonist and a plot which seemed to be moving at about the right pace. However, around half way through everything changes. This isn't be so bad in and of itself, at least if the rest of the book eventually linked everything together. The problem is that it doesn't. About 20 pages from the end I became extremely suspect when none of the loose ends had been tied up. At this stage the reader is suddenly bombarded with shedloads of extraneous information, history and NEW CHARACTERS (?!) which are meant to tie the plot together. <br /><br />The ending was meant to be a big Fight Club style reveal I think, but it just left me completely cold. Mainly because the cringe-worthy faux-philosophical/psychological ramblings which pepper the second half of the narrative, coupled with the feeling of being ushered clumsily out of the novel had left me pretty pissed off. The whole thing reminded me of a precocious ten year old schoolchild who has written a wonderful story with great characters and plots, but rushed the ending because their attention-span faltered. Having said all this I've given it 3/5 because in spite of all of the above, I never felt like putting it down. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15094401607470987024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/128642.The_Straw_Men"><img alt="The Straw Men (Straw Men #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1309212413l/128642._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4ScR5RIhzLTlBYg7GFbQd7FK1UAWNcGwBOJ4BOP8/7dXRGLurpXwRnu3Xp88zrcKK6KX+8iQMRWKtyufVB9TMg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sjqbPXLGl4eYR0gsVw+Wzhz2sLZhe3Favhlum3SVvi0EWeg2znKrdQb1nohzl/Gzhh7yDb/egf8wTD0Aw3YSqA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10056752731787636625">Michael Marshall (Smith) is a bestselling novelist and screenwriter. His first novel, ONLY FORWARD, won the August Derleth and Philip K. Dick awards. SPARES and ONE OF US were optioned for film by DreamWorks and Warner Brothers, and the Straw Men trilogy - THE STRAW MEN, THE LONELY DEAD and BLOOD OF ANGELS - were international bestsellers. His most recent novels are THE INTRUDERS, BAD THINGS and K</span>
  <span id="freeText10056752731787636625" style="display:none">Michael Marshall (Smith) is a bestselling novelist and screenwriter. His first novel, ONLY FORWARD, won the August Derleth and Philip K. Dick awards. SPARES and ONE OF US were optioned for film by DreamWorks and Warner Brothers, and the Straw Men trilogy - THE STRAW MEN, THE LONELY DEAD and BLOOD OF ANGELS - were international bestsellers. His most recent novels are THE INTRUDERS, BAD THINGS and KILLER MOVE. <br /><br />He is a four-time winner of the BFS Award for short fiction, and his stories are collected in two volumes - WHAT YOU MAKE IT and MORE TOMORROW AND OTHER STORIES (which won the International Horror Guild Award). <br /><br />He lives in Santa Cruz, California with his wife and son.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/trivia/work/123899-only-forward">Trivia About Only Forward</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
        <div class="mediumText">No trivia or quizzes yet. <a href="/trivia/work/123899-only-forward">Add some now &raquo;</a></div>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>


      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/123899-only-forward">Quotes from Only Forward</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;How many times have you tried to talk to someone about something that matters to you, tried to get them to see it the way you do? And how many of those times have ended with you feeling bitter, resenting them for making you feel like your pain doesn't have any substance after all?<br /><br />Like when you've split up with someone, and you try to communicate the way you feel, because you need to say the words, need to feel that somebody understands just how pissed off and frightened you feel. The problem is, they never do. "Plenty more fish in the sea," they'll say, or "You're better off without them," or "Do you want some of these potato chips?" They never really understand, because they haven't been there, every day, every hour. They don't know the way things have been, the way that it's made you, the way it has structured your world. They'll never realise that someone who makes you feel bad may be the person you need most in the world. They don't understand the history, the background, don't know the pillars of memory that hold you up. Ultimately, they don't know you well enough, and they never can. Everyone's alone in their world, because everybody's life is different. You can send people letters, and show them photos, but they can never come to visit where you live.<br /><br />Unless you love them. And then they can burn it down.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/152446-how-many-times-have-you-tried-to-talk-to-someone">706 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;When you're born a light is switched on, a light which shines up through your life. As you get older the light still reaches you, sparkling as it comes up through your memories. And if you're lucky as you travel forward through time, you'll bring the whole of yourself along with you, gathering your skirts and leaving nothing behind, nothing to obscure the light. But if a Bad Thing happens part of you is seared into place, and trapped for ever at that time. The rest of you moves onward, dealing with all the todays and tomorrows, but something, some part of you, is left behind. That part blocks the light, colours the rest of your life, but worse than that, it's alive. Trapped for ever at that moment, and alone in the dark, that part of you is still alive.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/519164-when-you-re-born-a-light-is-switched-on-a-light">90 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/123899-only-forward">More quotes&hellip;</a>
